Data Load¶

In [ ]:
import pandas as pd

GroupActivity = pd.read_csv("https://storage.googleapis.com/datalynn-datasets/interview-challenge/technology/Meta_Facebook_Groups_Community_Building/GroupActivity.csv")
GroupInfo = pd.read_csv("https://storage.googleapis.com/datalynn-datasets/interview-challenge/technology/Meta_Facebook_Groups_Community_Building/GroupInfo.csv")

Solution¶

Question 1:¶

Facebook aims to increase user engagement through group suggestions. Given the GroupActivity table, how would you develop an algorithm or model to recommend groups to users based on their interaction types and content they engage with? What features would be essential for this task?

Solution To recommend groups to users based on their interaction types and content they engage with, we need to devise a model that captures both the past behavior of users and the characteristics of the groups. Here's a step-by-step solution:

  1. Feature Engineering:

User Features:

  1. User Interaction Types Counts: For each user, calculate the count of each type of interaction (post, comment, like).
  2. User Content Keywords: Extract keywords from the content a user interacts with using techniques like TF-IDF.

Group Features:

  1. Group Interaction Types Counts: For each group, calculate the count of each type of interaction.
  2. Group Content Keywords: Extract keywords from the content posted in each group using techniques like TF-IDF.

User-Group Interaction:

  1. User-Group Interaction Count: How many interactions a user has had in a particular group.

  2. User-Group Content Overlap: Measure overlap between user's content keywords and group's content keywords.

  3. Model Design:

Collaborative Filtering: One common approach is collaborative filtering, where you can predict a user's interest in a group based on similar users' interest in that group.

Content-based Filtering: Another approach is content-based filtering, where recommendations are made based on user's past interactions.

For this task, a hybrid model combining both collaborative and content-based filtering would be beneficial.

In [ ]:
from sklearn.feature_extraction.text import TfidfVectorizer
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import cosine_similarity
import pandas as pd


# Convert data to DataFrames
group_activity_df = GroupActivity
group_info_df = GroupInfo

# Extract user content keywords
tfidf_vectorizer = TfidfVectorizer(max_features=1000, stop_words='english')
user_content_tfidf = tfidf_vectorizer.fit_transform(group_activity_df.groupby('user_id')['content'].apply(' '.join))
group_content_tfidf = tfidf_vectorizer.fit_transform(group_activity_df.groupby('group_id')['content'].apply(' '.join))

# Calculate user-group content overlap
content_overlap = cosine_similarity(user_content_tfidf, group_content_tfidf)

# Collaborative filtering based on interaction counts
user_group_interaction = pd.crosstab(group_activity_df['user_id'], group_activity_df['group_id'])

# Combine content overlap and collaborative filtering
alpha = 0.7
combined_score = alpha * content_overlap + (1-alpha) * user_group_interaction.values

# Recommend groups for users
recommendations = {}
for user_idx, user_id in enumerate(group_activity_df['user_id'].unique()):
    recommended_group_indices = combined_score[user_idx].argsort()[-5:][::-1]
    recommended_group_ids = [group_info_df.iloc[idx]['group_id'] for idx in recommended_group_indices]
    recommendations[user_id] = recommended_group_ids

print(recommendations)

Question 2:¶

Facebook aims to study group dynamics over time. Utilizing the GroupInfo and GroupActivity tables, assess the relationship between the group_category and the average number of interactions over months. How would this data assist in shaping Facebook's group promotion strategies?

In [ ]:
import pandas as pd

# Assuming you have two dataframes df_group_activity and df_group_info
# representing the GroupActivity and GroupInfo tables respectively.

# Merge the two dataframes on group_id
merged_df = pd.merge(group_activity_df, group_info_df, on='group_id')

# Convert activity_date column to datetime type
merged_df['activity_date'] = pd.to_datetime(merged_df['activity_date'])

# Extract the month and year from activity_date
merged_df['year_month'] = merged_df['activity_date'].dt.to_period('M')

# Group by group_category and year_month and calculate average number of interactions
avg_interactions = (merged_df.groupby(['group_category', 'year_month'])
                    .size()
                    .groupby(level=0)
                    .mean()
                    .reset_index(name='avg_interactions_per_month'))

print(avg_interactions)

  group_category  avg_interactions_per_month
0        Cooking                  114.071429
1        Fashion                  103.857143
2        Fitness                  123.714286
3          Music                  124.142857
4     Technology                  107.571429
5         Travel                  140.928571

This data can assist in shaping Facebook's group promotion strategies in the following ways:

  1. Targeted Promotion: By identifying categories with higher interactions, Facebook can promote these active groups to users who may be interested in those categories, leading to enhanced user engagement.

  2. Resource Allocation: Facebook can allocate more resources (like ad budget or feature development) towards the group categories that are more active and engaging.

  3. Category Boosting: If certain group categories have lower interactions, Facebook can roll out strategies to boost these categories, like organizing challenges or events related to those categories.

  4. Personalization: The data can be used to personalize the user's experience, showing them more content from categories where they are likely to interact more.

  5. Future Features: By understanding the interaction patterns, Facebook can develop and roll out new features that cater specifically to the needs of the most engaging group categories.

Question 3:¶

After assessing the group dynamics, a curious observation surfaces: certain categories have groups that are very active even if they were created recently, while some older groups witness dwindling activity. Using the GroupInfo and GroupActivity tables, delve into this observation. Highlight patterns and suggest potential product changes to revitalize older groups. Solutions To analyze group dynamics and highlight patterns between group category, group age, and activity level, we can proceed in the following way:

  1. Compute Group Age: For each group in the GroupInfo table, we can calculate its age in days.
  2. Compute Group Activity: Count the number of activities per group from the GroupActivity table over a recent time period (e.g., last 30 days).
  3. Merge the Data: Join the computed data from the above steps with the GroupInfo table to relate group age, group category, and recent activity.
  4. Analyze: Group by category and compute the average age of groups and average recent activity to see patterns.
In [ ]:
import pandas as pd

# Sample data (you would typically load this from a CSV or database)
group_info = group_info_df.copy()
group_activity = group_activity_df.copy()

# Step 1: Compute Group Age
group_info['group_creation_date'] = pd.to_datetime(group_info['group_creation_date'])
group_activity['activity_date'] = pd.to_datetime(group_activity['activity_date'])

group_info['group_age'] = (pd.Timestamp.now() - group_info['group_creation_date']).dt.days

# Step 2: Compute Group Activity
# Assuming "recent" means the last 30 days
latest_date = group_activity['activity_date'].max()
one_month_ago = latest_date - pd.Timedelta(days=30)

recent_activity = group_activity[group_activity['activity_date'] > one_month_ago]
activity_count = recent_activity.groupby('group_id').size().reset_index(name='recent_activity_count')

# Step 3: Merge the Data
merged_data = pd.merge(group_info, activity_count, on='group_id', how='left')
merged_data['recent_activity_count'].fillna(0, inplace=True)

# Step 4: Analyze
analysis = merged_data.groupby('group_category').agg(
    avg_group_age=('group_age', 'mean'),
    avg_recent_activity=('recent_activity_count', 'mean')
).reset_index()

print(analysis.sort_values(by='avg_recent_activity', ascending=False))

# Here you can see patterns, for example, if certain categories have newer groups but high activity
# while other categories have older groups with low activity.

  group_category  avg_group_age  avg_recent_activity
2        Fitness   -2565.780347             0.745665
3          Music   -2779.260355             0.745562
0        Cooking   -1984.006211             0.739130
5         Travel   -2516.403061             0.709184
1        Fashion   -2367.631579             0.697368
4     Technology   -2861.778523             0.677852

Suggested Product Changes:

  1. Targeted Engagement: For older groups with dwindling activity, introduce features like "Throwback Posts" or "Memory Lanes" to reminisce about older posts and rekindle engagement.
  2. Recommendation Algorithms: Suggest older groups to newer users who have shown interest in similar categories.
  3. Revitalize Feature: Introduce a "revitalize" feature where group admins can opt to "re-launch" their group, giving it a fresh start and higher visibility in the platform for a limited time.
  4. Feedback Loop: Allow users to provide feedback on why they might not be active in older groups. This can offer insights for further improvements.
  5. Diverse Content: Encourage diversity in content by prompting users to post different types of content in older groups.
  6. Notifications: Send out regular reminders or notifications to members of older groups about group milestones or trending topics to re-engage them.
